## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology
**Analysis**: The task belongs to population ecology, where dP_dt is the instantaneous population growth rate. It is typically modeled as a function of current population size P and sometimes time t, incorporating mechanisms like exponential growth, density-dependent regulation (logistic, Gompertz, theta-logistic), Allee effects, time-varying environments, or harvesting.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth when resources are abundant)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (density-dependent regulation with a carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - log(P)) (asymmetric slowdown near carrying capacity, often used for tumor or population growth)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**c2 (flexible density dependence with shape parameter c2 > 1)
- von Bertalanffy growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (allometric growth with linear loss, common in individual/body size growth applied to populations)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (scaling growth without carrying capacity, P ~ t^{1/(1-c1)} if c1≠1)
- Allee effect (cubic model): dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 - c2 * P**3 (growth rate negative at low and high densities, positive at intermediate, creating a critical population threshold)
- Time-varying environment with periodic forcing: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (seasonal fluctuations in intrinsic growth rate)
- Exponentially decaying environment: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(-c1 * t) (growth rate declines over time due to environmental deterioration)
- Harvesting or constant mortality: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 (logistic growth with fixed removal rate)
- Cubic density-dependent mortality: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 * P**3 (higher-order competition effects)
- Time-modulated logistic growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * P - c3 * P**2 (carrying capacity or growth rate oscillates with time)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative quadratic term -c1*P**2 in dP_dt indicates intraspecific competition or self-limiting density dependence
- Positive quadratic term +c1*P**2 combined with a negative cubic term -c2*P**3 suggests an Allee effect with a population threshold
- The term P * log(P) points to Gompertz-type growth with an asymmetric approach to carrying capacity
- Presence of sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) implies seasonal or periodic environmental forcing on the population growth rate
- Linear term +c0*P alone indicates exponential growth tendency when no density feedback is present
- A constant negative term -c2 in dP_dt reflects density-independent removal such as constant harvesting or natural mortality
- A multiplicative factor like exp(-c1*t) or sin(c2*t) acting on P indicates a time-varying intrinsic growth rate, often due to environmental change
- Power-law terms P**c1 with c1 ≠ 1 suggest allometric scaling between growth rate and population size, typical in size-structured or metabolic-based population models
- A sum of P, P**2, P**3 with alternating signs can capture multiple fixed points (e.g., extinction, unstable equilibrium, carrying capacity) characteristic of metastable populations

**GT:** `0.7124*P^(1/3) + 0.7124*(1 - P/68.906)*P + 0.7124*P*exp(-0.03459*t)`

Expanding: `0.7124*P^(1/3) + 0.7124*P - 0.7124/68.906 * P^2 + 0.7124*P*exp(-0.03459*t)`

So GT = `c_a * P^(1/3) + c_b * P^2 + c_c * P + c_d * P * exp(c_e * t)`

where c_a = 0.7124, c_b = -0.7124/68.906 ≈ -0.01034, c_c = 0.7124, c_d = 0.7124, c_e = -0.03459.

The GT has exactly these basis functions: **P^(1/3), P^2, P, P·exp(αt)** and no additive constant.
